# LeetCode Problems with Easily Obtainable Testcases

Generated June 9, 2026 from 3,958 problems returned by LeetCode's public GraphQL catalog.

## Method

This report looks for problems whose complete valid top-level input domain is small enough to enumerate locally. It prioritizes problems that also suit lazy, Haskell-like solutions: recursive generators, streams, algebraic trees, and recurrence sequences.

A small-looking constraint is not sufficient by itself. Every independent argument matters. For example, `n <= 9` is tiny, but a second argument ranging up to `n!` creates hundreds of thousands of valid calls.

This analysis uses published constraints, not LeetCode's hidden testcase collection. Enumerating every valid input gives complete behavioral coverage only when those constraints describe a genuinely finite and tractable domain.

## Misleadingly Small Constraints

| Problem | Approximate valid calls | Why it is larger than it looks |
|---|---:|---|
| [60. Permutation Sequence](https://leetcode.com/problems/permutation-sequence/) | 409,113 | `n <= 9`, but `k` ranges up to `n!` |
| [1238. Circular Permutation in Binary Representation](https://leetcode.com/problems/circular-permutation-in-binary-representation/) | 131,070 | `start` ranges across every `n`-bit value |
| [1545. Find Kth Bit in Nth Binary String](https://leetcode.com/problems/find-kth-bit-in-nth-binary-string/) | 1,048,554 | `k` ranges across a string of length `2^n - 1` |
| [779. K-th Symbol in Grammar](https://leetcode.com/problems/k-th-symbol-in-grammar/) | 1,073,741,793 | `k` has an exponential range |

The strongest first batch is:

22, 38, 51, 89, 95, 96, 118, 3211, 894, 17

Together these exercise lazy lists, recursive trees, unfolding, backtracking, recurrence streams, and demand-driven combinatorial generation while keeping the valid input domains tractable.

## Caveats

- LeetCode can change problem statements and constraints after this report date.
- Some catalog entries are contest or newer problems whose numbering is not contiguous.
- Output order may need canonicalization when LeetCode accepts answers in any order.
- For object-design problems, the input is an operation sequence rather than one simple argument tuple.
- Exhaustive inputs still require a trusted oracle to compute expected outputs.
